1 The Cat continued for two or three months thus to carry his Majesty , from time to time , game of his master 's taking .
2 One day in particular , when he knew for certain that he was to take the air along the river-side , with his daughter , the most beautiful princess in the world , he said to his master : `` If you will follow my advice your fortune is made .
3 You have nothing else to do but go and wash yourself in the river , in that part I shall show you , and leave the rest to me . ''
4 The Marquis of Carabas did what the Cat advised him to , without knowing why or wherefore .
5 While he was washing the King passed by , and the Cat began to cry out : `` Help !
6 help !
7 My Lord Marquis of Carabas is going to be drowned . ''
8 At this noise the King put his head out of the coach-window , and , finding it was the Cat who had so often brought him such good game , he commanded his guards to run immediately to the assistance of his Lordship the Marquis of Carabas .
9 While they were drawing the poor Marquis out of the river , the Cat came up to the coach and told the King that , while his master was washing , there came by some rogues , who went off with his clothes , though he had cried out : `` Thieves !
10 thieves ! ''
11 several times , as loud as he could .
12 This cunning Cat had hidden them under a great stone .
13 The King immediately commanded the officers of his wardrobe to run and fetch one of his best suits for the Lord Marquis of Carabas .
14 The King caressed him after a very extraordinary manner , and as the fine clothes he had given him extremely set off his good mien -LRB- for he was well made and very handsome in his person -RRB- , the King 's daughter took a secret inclination to him , and the Marquis of Carabas had no sooner cast two or three respectful and somewhat tender glances but she fell in love with him to distraction .
15 The King would needs have him come into the coach and take part of the airing .
16 The Cat , quite overjoyed to see his project begin to succeed , marched on before , and , meeting with some countrymen , who were mowing a meadow , he said to them : `` Good people , you who are mowing , if you do not tell the King that the meadow you mow belongs to my Lord Marquis of Carabas , you shall be chopped as small as herbs for the pot . ''
17 The King did not fail asking of the mowers to whom the meadow they were mowing belonged .
18 `` To my Lord Marquis of Carabas , '' answered they altogether , for the Cat 's threats had made them terribly afraid .
19 `` You see , sir , '' said the Marquis , `` this is a meadow which never fails to yield a plentiful harvest every year . ''
20 The Master Cat , who went still on before , met with some reapers , and said to them : `` Good people , you who are reaping , if you do not tell the King that all this corn belongs to the Marquis of Carabas , you shall be chopped as small as herbs for the pot . ''
21 The King , who passed by a moment after , would XXXXX know to whom all that corn , which he then saw , did belong .	needs		Lordship|Marquis|air|head|master|mien|needs|person|river|thieves

17 The Cat , who had taken care to inform himself who this ogre was and what he could do , asked to speak with him , saying he could not pass so near his castle without having the honor of paying his respects to him .
18 The ogre received him as civilly as an ogre could do , and made him sit down .
19 `` I have been assured , '' said the Cat , `` that you have the gift of being able to change yourself into all sorts of creatures you have a mind to ; you can , for example , transform yourself into a lion , or elephant , and the like . ''
20 `` That is true , '' answered the ogre very briskly ; `` and to convince you , you shall see me now become a lion . ''

12 The Cat , who had taken care to inform himself who this ogre was and what he could do , asked to speak with him , saying he could not pass so near his castle without having the honor of paying his respects to him .
13 The ogre received him as civilly as an ogre could do , and made him sit down .
14 `` I have been assured , '' said the Cat , `` that you have the gift of being able to change yourself into all sorts of creatures you have a mind to ; you can , for example , transform yourself into a lion , or elephant , and the like . ''
15 `` That is true , '' answered the ogre very briskly ; `` and to convince you , you shall see me now become a lion . ''
16 Puss was so sadly terrified at the sight of a lion so near him that he immediately got into the gutter , not without abundance of trouble and danger , because of his boots , which were of no use at all to him in walking upon the tiles .
17 A little while after , when Puss saw that the ogre had resumed his natural form , he came down , and owned he had been very much frightened .
18 `` I have been , moreover , informed , '' said the Cat , `` but I know not how to believe it , that you have also the power to take on you the shape of the smallest animals ; for example , to change yourself into a rat or a mouse ; but I must own to you I take this to be impossible . ''
19 `` Impossible ! ''
20 cried the ogre ; `` you shall see that presently . ''
21 And at the same time he changed himself into a XXXXX , and began to run about the floor .	mouse		Marquis|care|daughter|gift|herbs|master|moment|mouse|people|sight

1 The Cat , quite overjoyed to see his project begin to succeed , marched on before , and , meeting with some countrymen , who were mowing a meadow , he said to them : `` Good people , you who are mowing , if you do not tell the King that the meadow you mow belongs to my Lord Marquis of Carabas , you shall be chopped as small as herbs for the pot . ''
2 The King did not fail asking of the mowers to whom the meadow they were mowing belonged .
3 `` To my Lord Marquis of Carabas , '' answered they altogether , for the Cat 's threats had made them terribly afraid .
4 `` You see , sir , '' said the Marquis , `` this is a meadow which never fails to yield a plentiful harvest every year . ''
5 The Master Cat , who went still on before , met with some reapers , and said to them : `` Good people , you who are reaping , if you do not tell the King that all this corn belongs to the Marquis of Carabas , you shall be chopped as small as herbs for the pot . ''
6 The King , who passed by a moment after , would needs know to whom all that corn , which he then saw , did belong .
7 `` To my Lord Marquis of Carabas , '' replied the reapers , and the King was very well pleased with it , as well as the Marquis , whom he congratulated thereupon .
8 The Master Cat , who went always before , said the same words to all he met , and the King was astonished at the vast estates of my Lord Marquis of Carabas .
9 Monsieur Puss came at last to a stately castle , the master of which was an ogre , the richest had ever been known ; for all the lands which the King had then gone over belonged to this castle .
10 The Cat , who had taken care to inform himself who this ogre was and what he could do , asked to speak with him , saying he could not pass so near his castle without having the honor of paying his respects to him .
11 The ogre received him as civilly as an ogre could do , and made him sit down .
12 `` I have been assured , '' said the Cat , `` that you have the gift of being able to change yourself into all sorts of creatures you have a mind to ; you can , for example , transform yourself into a lion , or elephant , and the like . ''
13 `` That is true , '' answered the ogre very briskly ; `` and to convince you , you shall see me now become a lion . ''
14 Puss was so sadly terrified at the sight of a lion so near him that he immediately got into the gutter , not without abundance of trouble and danger , because of his boots , which were of no use at all to him in walking upon the tiles .
15 A little while after , when Puss saw that the ogre had resumed his natural form , he came down , and owned he had been very much frightened .
16 `` I have been , moreover , informed , '' said the Cat , `` but I know not how to believe it , that you have also the power to take on you the shape of the smallest animals ; for example , to change yourself into a rat or a mouse ; but I must own to you I take this to be impossible . ''
17 `` Impossible ! ''
18 cried the ogre ; `` you shall see that presently . ''
19 And at the same time he changed himself into a mouse , and began to run about the floor .
20 Puss no sooner perceived this but he fell upon him and ate him up .
21 Meanwhile the King , who saw , as he passed , this fine XXXXX of the ogre 's , had a mind to go into it .	castle		Lord|animals|castle|countrymen|form|lands|meadow|moment|pot|words

14 Puss , who heard the noise of his Majesty 's coach running over the draw-bridge , ran out , and said to the King : `` Your Majesty is welcome to this castle of my Lord Marquis of Carabas . ''
15 `` What !
16 my Lord Marquis , '' cried the King , `` and does this castle also belong to you ?
17 There can be nothing finer than this court and all the stately buildings which surround it ; let us go into it , if you please . ''
18 The Marquis gave his hand to the Princess , and followed the King , who went first .
19 They passed into a spacious hall , where they found a magnificent collation , which the ogre had prepared for his friends , who were that very day to visit him , but dared not to enter , knowing the King was there .
20 His Majesty was perfectly charmed with the good qualities of my Lord Marquis of Carabas , as was his daughter , who had fallen violently in love with him , and , seeing the vast estate he possessed , said to him , after having drunk five or six glasses : `` It will be owing to yourself only , my Lord Marquis , if you are not my son-in-law . ''
21 The Marquis , making several low bows , accepted the honor which his XXXXX conferred upon him , and forthwith , that very same day , married the Princess .	Majesty		Majesty|hall|honor|love|mind|noise|power|rat|respects|time

1 A little while after , when Puss saw that the ogre had resumed his natural form , he came down , and owned he had been very much frightened .
2 `` I have been , moreover , informed , '' said the Cat , `` but I know not how to believe it , that you have also the power to take on you the shape of the smallest animals ; for example , to change yourself into a rat or a mouse ; but I must own to you I take this to be impossible . ''
3 `` Impossible ! ''
4 cried the ogre ; `` you shall see that presently . ''
5 And at the same time he changed himself into a mouse , and began to run about the floor .
6 Puss no sooner perceived this but he fell upon him and ate him up .
7 Meanwhile the King , who saw , as he passed , this fine castle of the ogre 's , had a mind to go into it .
8 Puss , who heard the noise of his Majesty 's coach running over the draw-bridge , ran out , and said to the King : `` Your Majesty is welcome to this castle of my Lord Marquis of Carabas . ''
9 `` What !
10 my Lord Marquis , '' cried the King , `` and does this castle also belong to you ?
11 There can be nothing finer than this court and all the stately buildings which surround it ; let us go into it , if you please . ''
12 The Marquis gave his hand to the Princess , and followed the King , who went first .
13 They passed into a spacious hall , where they found a magnificent collation , which the ogre had prepared for his friends , who were that very day to visit him , but dared not to enter , knowing the King was there .
14 His Majesty was perfectly charmed with the good qualities of my Lord Marquis of Carabas , as was his daughter , who had fallen violently in love with him , and , seeing the vast estate he possessed , said to him , after having drunk five or six glasses : `` It will be owing to yourself only , my Lord Marquis , if you are not my son-in-law . ''
15 The Marquis , making several low bows , accepted the honor which his Majesty conferred upon him , and forthwith , that very same day , married the Princess .
16 Puss became a great lord , and never ran after mice any more but only for his diversion .

20 When she went away she said to me : '' ` Be careful of my gifts , good man ; see that you do not lose the ring or forget to water the pinks .

16 Be very sure that I will take care of you , and water you well , and never allow any cruel hand to tear you from your stems . ''
17 As she leaned over them she noticed that they were very dry .
18 So taking her pitcher , she ran off in the clear moonlight to the fountain , which was at some distance .
19 When she reached it she sat down upon the brink to rest , but she had hardly done so when she saw a stately lady coming toward her , surrounded by numbers of attendants .
20 Six maids of honor carried her train , and she leaned upon the arm of another .
21 When they came near the XXXXX a canopy was spread for her , under which was placed a sofa of cloth-of-gold , and presently a dainty supper was served , upon a table covered with dishes of gold and crystal , while the wind in the trees and the falling water of the fountain murmured the softest music .	fountain		care|child|everything|fountain|gifts|honor|marsh|nothing|pitcher|scent

9 Felicia , who was very gentle , said nothing , but stood up crying quietly ; while Bruno , for that was her brother 's name , sat comfortably by the fire .
10 Presently , when supper-time came , Bruno had a delicious egg , and he threw the shell to Felicia , saying : `` There , that is all I can give you ; if you do n't like it , go out and catch frogs ; there are plenty of them in the marsh close by . ''
11 Felicia did not answer , but she cried more bitterly than ever , and went away to her own little room .
12 She found it filled with the sweet scent of the pinks , and , going up to them , she said sadly : `` Beautiful pinks , you are so sweet and so pretty , you are the only comfort I have left .
13 Be very sure that I will take care of you , and water you well , and never allow any cruel hand to tear you from your stems . ''
14 As she leaned over them she noticed that they were very dry .
15 So taking her pitcher , she ran off in the clear moonlight to the fountain , which was at some distance .
16 When she reached it she sat down upon the brink to rest , but she had hardly done so when she saw a stately lady coming toward her , surrounded by numbers of attendants .
17 Six maids of honor carried her train , and she leaned upon the arm of another .
18 When they came near the fountain a canopy was spread for her , under which was placed a sofa of cloth-of-gold , and presently a dainty supper was served , upon a table covered with dishes of gold and crystal , while the wind in the trees and the falling water of the fountain murmured the softest music .
19 Felicia was hidden in the shade , too much astonished by all she saw to venture to move ; but in a few moments the Queen said : `` I fancy I see a shepherdess near that tree ; bid her come hither . ''
20 So Felicia came forward and saluted the Queen timidly , but with so much grace that all were surprised .
21 `` What are you doing here , my pretty XXXXX ? ''	child		child|fountain|grace|life|man|mother|possessions|shade|tree|venture

15 `` I want to know what you were doing at the fountain so late ? ''
16 said the Queen presently .
17 `` I came to fetch a pitcher of water for my pinks , madam , '' she answered , stooping to pick up the pitcher which stood beside her ; but when she showed it to the Queen she was amazed to see that it had turned to gold , all sparkling with great diamonds , and the water , of which it was full , was more fragrant than the sweetest roses .

14 `` I came to fetch a pitcher of water for my pinks , madam , '' she answered , stooping to pick up the pitcher which stood beside her ; but when she showed it to the Queen she was amazed to see that it had turned to gold , all sparkling with great diamonds , and the water , of which it was full , was more fragrant than the sweetest roses .

20 So Felicia took up her pitcher and ran to her little room , but while she had been away Bruno had gone in and taken the pot of pinks , leaving a great cabbage in its place .

5 `` But tell me , have you supped ? ''
6 `` No , madam , '' answered Felicia ; `` my brother ate all the supper there was . ''
7 Then the Queen ordered that a place should be made for her at the table , and herself loaded Felicia 's plate with good things ; but she was too much astonished to be hungry .
8 `` I want to know what you were doing at the fountain so late ? ''
9 said the Queen presently .
10 `` I came to fetch a pitcher of water for my pinks , madam , '' she answered , stooping to pick up the pitcher which stood beside her ; but when she showed it to the Queen she was amazed to see that it had turned to gold , all sparkling with great diamonds , and the water , of which it was full , was more fragrant than the sweetest roses .
11 She was afraid to take it until the Queen said : `` It is yours , Felicia ; go and water your pinks with it , and let it remind you that the Queen of the Woods is your friend . ''
12 The shepherdess threw herself at the Queen 's feet , and thanked her humbly for her gracious words .
13 `` Ah !
14 madam , '' she cried , `` if I might beg you to stay here a moment I would run and fetch my pot of pinks for you -- they could not fall into better hands . ''
15 `` Go , Felicia , '' said the Queen , stroking her cheek softly ; `` I will wait here until you come back . ''
16 So Felicia took up her pitcher and ran to her little room , but while she had been away Bruno had gone in and taken the pot of pinks , leaving a great cabbage in its place .
17 When she saw the unlucky cabbage Felicia was much distressed , and did not know what to do ; but at last she ran back to the fountain , and , kneeling before the Queen , said : `` Madam , Bruno has stolen my pot of pinks , so I have nothing but my silver ring ; but I beg you to accept it as a proof of my gratitude . ''
18 `` But if I take your ring , my pretty shepherdess , '' said the Queen , `` you will have nothing left ; and what will you do then ? ''
19 `` Ah !
20 madam , '' she answered simply , `` if I have your friendship I shall do very well . ''
21 So the Queen took the XXXXX and put it on her finger , and mounted her chariot , which was made of coral studded with emeralds , and drawn by six milk-white horses .	ring		care|heart|nothing|pinks|pitcher|plate|ring|room|supper|table

8 As soon as it was light , Felicia , who was very unhappy about her pot of pinks , went out to look for it , and the first thing she found was the unfortunate cabbage .
9 She gave it a push with her foot , saying : `` What are you doing here , and how dared you put yourself in the place of my pot of pinks ? ''
10 `` If I had n't been carried , '' replied the cabbage , `` you may be very sure that I should n't have thought of going there . ''
11 It made her shiver with fright to hear the cabbage talk , but he went on : `` If you will be good enough to plant me by my comrades again , I can tell you where your pinks are at this moment -- hidden in Bruno 's bed ! ''
12 Felicia was in despair when she heard this , not knowing how she was to get them back .
13 But she replanted the cabbage very kindly in his old place , and , as she finished doing it , she saw Bruno 's hen , and said , catching hold of it : `` Come here , horrid little creature !
14 you shall suffer for all the unkind things my brother has done to me . ''
15 `` Ah !
16 shepherdess , '' said the hen , `` do n't kill me ; I am rather a gossip , and I can tell you some surprising things that you will like to hear .
17 Do n't imagine that you are the daughter of the poor laborer who brought you up ; your mother was a queen who had six girls already , and the King threatened that unless she had a son who could inherit his kingdom she should have her head cut off .
18 `` So when the Queen had another little daughter she was quite frightened , and agreed with her sister -LRB- who was a fairy -RRB- to exchange her for the fairy 's little son .
19 Now the Queen had been shut up in a great tower by the King 's orders , and when a great many days went by and still she heard nothing from the Fairy she made her escape from the window by means of a rope ladder , taking her little baby with her .
20 After wandering about until she was half dead with cold and fatigue she reached this cottage .

5 After seeking me everywhere he believed that I must have been drowned , or eaten up by wild beasts in the forest .
6 That same lady came here once more , and commanded that you should be called Felicia , and left the ring and the pot of pinks to be given to you ; and while she was in the house twenty-five of the King 's guards came to search for you , doubtless meaning to kill you ; but she muttered a few words , and immediately they all turned into cabbages .
7 It was one of them whom you threw out of your window yesterday .
8 `` I do n't know how it was that he could speak -- I have never heard either of them say a word before , nor have I been able to do it myself until now . ''
9 The Princess was greatly astonished at the hen 's story , and said kindly : `` I am truly sorry for you , my poor nurse , and wish it was in my power to restore you to your real form .
10 But we must not despair ; it seems to me , after what you have told me , that something must be going to happen soon .
11 Just now , however , I must go and look for my pinks , which I love better than anything in the world . ''
12 Bruno had gone out into the forest , never thinking that Felicia would search in his room for the pinks , and she was delighted by his unexpected absence , and thought to get them back without further trouble .
13 But as soon as she entered the room she saw a terrible army of rats , who were guarding the straw bed ; and when she attempted to approach it they sprang at her , biting and scratching furiously .
14 Quite terrified , she drew back , crying out : `` Oh !
15 my dear pinks , how can you stay here in such bad company ? ''
16 Then she suddenly bethought herself of the pitcher of water , and , hoping that it might have some magic power , she ran to fetch it , and sprinkled a few drops over the fierce-looking swarm of rats .
17 In a moment not a tail or a whisker was to be seen .
18 Each one had made for his hole as fast as his legs could carry him , so that the Princess could safely take her pot of pinks .
19 She found them nearly dying for want of water , and hastily poured all that was left in the pitcher upon them .
20 As she bent over them , enjoying their delicious scent , a soft voice , that seemed to rustle among the leaves , said : `` Lovely Felicia , the day has come at last when I may have the happiness of telling you how even the flowers love you and rejoice in your beauty . ''
